< Review>
Appalling and horrendous.  That's the only way to describe my experience.  Yesterday, as I was riding my bike past Dr. Domotor's around 4:45pm, I noticed that there was a dead parrot in the grass in front of the "Animal Hospital".  I figured some low-life that couldn't be bothered to properly dispose of it had left it there to make it another person's problem.  Well, it became mine.

I went inside and told the lady at the front desk that there was a dead parrot outside of the building.  When she looked at me like she didn't know what to do, I offered to bring it inside if she gave me a box and a pair of gloves.  A lady came out in scrubs, and the first lady asked her if she would take care of it.  Her response was "I'm off the clock.  Can't you call Animal Control?"  The first lady then thanked me for telling them and assured me they would take care of it.

Well, I guess everyone was off the clock.  They didn't do anything, not even call Animal Control.  In this case, that would be the Pasadena Humane Society and SPCA.  I called them this morning after I walked past the building and the bird was still there.  When I called Dr. Domotor's to let them know what happened, I didn't even get a response, they just hung up on me without saying anything.

To make it clear, I would have been willing to take care of the bird myself in other circumstances.  Years ago, driving past a restaurant I worked at (on my day off), I noticed a dead cat in the road in front of the building.  I stopped, borrowed a shovel, and buried the cat away from the building.  Had I not, there's no telling how long it would have been there.  It's also less likely that the litter of kittens with her, which were still alive, would have been saved.  I don't usually carry a shovel on my bike, and I wasn't about to put a dead parrot in my pocket so I could rub it with my thumb like Lenny Small.

I also understand that you might be wary about a dead animal, and want to take certain precautions before exposing it to other animals.  There is absolutely no excuse for just leaving a dead animal in front of an "Animal Hospital" overnight, or even for ten minutes.  Perhaps at least somebody there has a brain and genuine concern for animals, but at least three don't.  If you take your pets there, good luck with the ones that end up handling them.< /Review>

<Time>1326839930107<//Time><Rating>1<//Rating>< Text>
Domotor's Doggie Dachau

I left my 10 1/2 year old spayed Lab for three nights kenneling.  I took two standard bed pillows in sewn-together cases, a cotton throw rug that goes on top of the pillows, and in a large zip-lock a T-shirt I'd worn to provide my scent, a squeaky toy, and several large crunchy bones. I verbally asked them to place the pillow in her kennel and to give the dog the T-shirt, squeaky toy, and one crunchy bone per day.  The assistant acknowledged this.  The vet's assistant removed my dog's collar and scarf and gave them to me, saying they could be a choke hazard.  (It's the first time I'd had this occur for kenneling - there must have been a tragic experience in the past, but better safe than sorry)  I inspected the individual kennel my dog was in.  It was very clean and had a clean blanket on the concrete floor.  I was not allowed to open the gate and place the pillows inside, but was assured my dog would have them.

After the three nights I returned for my dog.  The dog was as healthy as when I left her.  I put her collar back on and asked for the pillows, T-shirt, etc. In a jiffy the assistant returned with the pillows, rug, and zip-lock.  The zip-lock contained the T-shirt, squeaky toy, and ALL of the crunchy bones.  The T-shirt, pillows, and rug had no dog hair on them.

I highly suspect that my pure bred, ACK-papers, house-dog had to sleep on a blanket over concrete with nothing to remind her of 10 1/2 years with her owner, or hope that she would be reunited with me.  My dog is healthy and Dr. Domnotor's kennel is very clean.  I have no complaint about the safety or sanitation of the kennels.  But I think I sent my dog to a Doggy Dachau.  She will not be kenneled there again.< /Text>

My mom has been going to Dr Demotor for 15 years. We moved during that time and have tried new vets that are closer. Every time we try a new vet we end up taking the animal back to Dr. Demotor because the other vets don't have the experience or knowledge about taking care of tricky issues. We have a dog with a gum infection we took her to another vet for 3 years and she lost over half her teeth. We got fed up and took her to Dr Domotor and the infection was clear within a few months. I have a cat who got into a fight. I tried taking her to VCA and they didnt find the puncture wounds. Because they didnt find the wounds the first time bacteria festered under her skin and now, a week later, she is loosing almost half of the skin on her back. The doctors at Dr Domotors office decided to take a skin culture to be sure that we were fighting the disease with the right antibiotics. No to mention they remembered to give me painkillers... Yea Dr. Domotor is expensive but it's a sure way to guarantee that your pet will get proper treatment by experienced professionals. You wont spend all your money visiting the vet for the same reason over and over. I hope they stay in business for as long as my cat will live.<//review>

<Date>1538060543667< /Date><rate>4</rate>< Text>
My first visit here to "Froyo Life". It seems to be a pretty well known place here in Los Angeles, and it seems to be a late night dessert place. My cousins actually took us here one night while visiting them down here in SoCal.

Most of the time, you'll probably be standing here in line, waiting and waiting for your turn to order since it's a small place, and seemingly very popular. With limited seating as well, only like a few tables inside and a few tables outside.

I ordered a "Triple Chocolate Shake", which was $6.50. It tasted pretty decent, chocolate galore haha.  My cousins and family ordered the Ice Cream Sandwiches or the macarons if you wanna call them that too.

We didn't have to look so hard for parking since my cousins lived nearby, but for others who don't quite have that luxury, parking will be a hassle for you seeing as they don't have their own parking lot.

Overall great first experience!</Text>

<rating>4</rating>< text>
Yes, each ice cream sandwich and ice cream bar is $5 (prior to tax), but it is very well worth the money.  However, if you're not a very big sweets fan, I recommend that you share an ice cream sandwich or bar with 1 other person or 2 other people.  Our family has only tried the Red Velvet ice cream sandwich, and one was sufficient for 3 people.  Again, we're not big fans of sweets unless the dessert involves a slice of good tiramisu or cheesecake.  The macaron of the ice cream sandwich is a bit on the sweet side (think Bottega Louie macarons), but it adds the right texture to the soft red velvet ice cream. Next time, I think my mom and I will try the pistachio ice cream in a cup.</text>

< text>
FroYo Life is a Montrose hangout. It's super popular on Friday and Saturday night. You'll find a lot of families and teens here.

It's a great snack and healthier alternative to ice cream. There's a dozen different flavors of FroYo and about 2 dozen different toppings from fruit to cookie dough and gummy bears.

On the real tho, FroYo Life... It's 60 degrees outside, night time and you're AC blasting the AC. You know it's freezing right? Don't be like that..</text>

< review>
These ice cream sandwiches are no joke. They're about the size of a fat hockey puck (yep, how Canadian of me to use that for comparison). I've tried the coffee, cookies and cream, red velvet, thai tea, and grasshopper macaron ice cream sandwiches and no, not by myself and not all in one sitting. It was TWO sittings, hah.  Since I'm a mint chocolate chip kinda girl, the grasshopper was my favorite with the thai tea running a close second.

Other desserts that I've sampled at Froyo Life are the blue velvet cake and the strawberry shortcake bar.  The blue velvet cake tasted like red velvet to me and was overall a bit too sweet for my taste. The strawberry shortcake bar was refreshing. I'd probably order this if the grasshopper macaron ice cream was unavailable.

Overall, a perfect destination if you have a sweet tooth.</review>

< text>
I can certainly understand how many feel displeased with their customer service. They have moved to using an answering service staffed with personnel all speaking of a foreign accent (I cannot verify but I would certainly bet that it isn't being done in the US). The first call I attempted lasted 2 hrs and 12 minutes. It took about 62 minutes to get to talk to a 'staff member' initially, who after verifying my account details then decided they could not assist me and that they would transfer me to another department. But rest assured it would be an immediate transfer... I kept the phone on speaker and waited some more, at the 2hr12min mark the line hung up. < review>
I waited around 6 weeks after my work was done to write this review because I wanted to make sure it was accurate. I brought my Honda Odyssey in for A/C repair work. Everything was going great until I needed one additional part. This part was on national backorder due the major shipping stoppages from Covid-19 from overseas. The biggest cost with A/C work is usually labor. It takes time and a specialized mechanic to do the work. Long story short SB Tire worked with me after I was able to find the part. The part was far away and needed time to get to Santa Barbara. After it arrived they were able to assemble everything perfectly and my A/C has never been better. Most places would have just sealed the hvac back up and charged me again for reopening it when the part arrived. This probably saved me around 1k. I would definitely recommend SB Tire. They are honest and do quality work at a very reasonable price. They also will go out of their way to try and save you money if the opportunity arrives. Props to them!< /review>

< Text>
Management is completely rude and money-thirsty. I called to re-activate my account that was canceled over two years ago. I was told over the phone that booking a lane for lap swimming was easier and that between 1pm and 3pm swimming for an hour was not going to be an issue, he even said ‚ÄúI guarantee‚Äù since I have some issues with my back I was advised by my doctor to swim. I explained over the phone that I was not interested neither able to do anything but lap pool.

But when I actually showed up to swim, after they charged my card with first and last month (I wasn‚Äôt even told that they were going to charge me for last month which is a higher fee than first month for some unknown reason) the reality was completely different. They don‚Äôt offer online or phone reservations for the pool. You must show up and and is just for half hour. The pool is indoor and not windows are open so I‚Äôm not sure they are in compliance with covid-19 protocols.

I immediately felt off, I did 20 minutes of swimming and I left. I went to Crunch Yerba Buena two days latter and they have outdoor pool with the ability to reserve a lane over the phone 24 hours ahead or same day for ONE hour. Membership is cheaper, you can change in the bathroom and they provide swimming robes so you don‚Äôt walk around in your swimming suit, etc. I called Fitness SF to cancel since they really are not offering what I was told. Their general manager Mr. Kevin Williams took the call after a long wait and told me from the start of the call that they don‚Äôt refund memberships after five days. <date>1553112941389</date><user_id>107950664407502898789<//user_id>< review>
The Fitness SF, Fillmore branch is my favorite gym in the city. The reason why is partly because of the gym features but mostly because of the people and the sense of community there.

The gym itself is modern, clean, and has all the equipment I need, including a pool, sauna and hot tub! There are many weekly classes available, and the gym's hours are reasonable. The trainers, however, are top-notch! They are always friendly, welcoming, and helpful. I've worked with Juancho, Rodrigo, and others there. They are all great!

Juancho teaches and trains TRX classes and one-on-one training sessions. His focus is core and full-body movement. After a couple classes with him, I am toned in a way that I cannot get to on my own -- he really pushes me to the next, well, next few levels. It's hard work but totally pays off. He's really good at catering a session to your needs and level. He also listens very well to me which I appreciate.

Rodrigo is much more focused on strength, and specific and particular areas of your body that needs a boost. I've worked with him on a couple one-on-one training sessions and thought he was a great trainer. Like Juancho, he also pushed  me to new limits. He has a very encouraging attitude which I find helpful and he's given me good tips that have been very useful.

Both of these guys are so positive and upbeat, it's great to work with them. I would like to work with them more. I would recommend them to anyone looking to strengthen and tone. I'd also recommend just about any trainer at the Fitness SF, Fillmore branch. It's a good place train and a great community.< /review>

< Text>
I've been going to this gym since the 1990's, paying dues religiously since (probably $20k in total) over 3 ownerships.  FitnessSF has really brought the club downhill.  The showers are always broken.  The swim suit spinner is always broken.  The shower outside pool used to be warm, now cold.  They removed carpets from the dressing rooms.  They replaced the normal towels with tiny dishtowel size ones, which they also don't clean as well.  They don't provide towels in the locker rooms, so they will only give you 2 at the front desk.  If you forget, or need one after undressing or in swim suit, you have to parade through the entire gym to the front desk to get another towel.

To top it off, they just increased dues by 17% and when I wrote to inquire about the increase, they cancelled my membership with no further interaction or confirmation from me.  Their Dir of Operations, Don Dickerson, appears to have had a real negative impact on the club (apparently, just short term view on numbers).

Check out the alternatives like USF Koret for awesome pool, and even public pools like Rossi or Mission pools.</Text>

< Review>
Updates: The "first month free" banner is still up and I have left the facility. My price increased once.

Overall a pretty pleasant experience. I was assisted by Mark who showed me the unit. Up front he disclosed there would be mandatory insurance added on top of the unit fee, and the website disclosed the one time admin fee, so there were no hidden fees by the time I signed the contract/lease. He even warned me ahead of time that the rent would most likely increase in approximately 5 months.

I do have a couple of concerns that lie with the company and its owner. When you drive up, there is a large banner stating "first month free", and upon mentioning it to the employees I am told that this promo is no longer active and they are not allowed to take the banner down. Blatant fishing and false advertisement. Next, I don't know how the units are measured, but I'm renting a 5x5 and when I think that, I think 5 wide x 5 deep. I'm 5'3" and if I were to lie down in the unit I would stick out about halfway. It's more like 2.5 x 2.5.

The prices are a bit high because they take full advantage of the high demand for storage. Based on that I will probably leave the facility before the price goes up.</Review>
